So evaṃ vadeti – ‘kiṃ ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno? Kissāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti? Te evaṃ vadenti – ‘ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekā āpatti jānappaṭicchannā, ekā āpatti ajānappaṭicchannā. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tāyo ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno, tāsāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘yāyaṃ, āvuso, āpatti jānappaṭicchannā, dhammikaṃ tassā āpattiyā parivāsadānaṃ; dhammattā ruhati. Yā ca khvāyaṃ, āvuso, āpatti ajānappaṭicchannā, adhammikaṃ tassā āpattiyā parivāsadānaṃ; adhammattā na ruhati. Ekissā, āvuso, āpattiyā bhikkhu mānattāraho’’’ti.

144.“Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits two offenses entailing suspension, both concealed for two months—one offense concealed knowingly, the other concealed unknowingly. He asks the Saṅgha for two months’ probation for those offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him two months’ probation for those offenses concealed for two months. While he is undergoing probation, another bhikkhu arrives—learned, versed in the texts, a master of the Dhamma, a master of the Vinaya, a master of the Mātikā, wise, experienced, intelligent, conscientious, scrupulous, and desirous of training. He asks, ‘What offense has this bhikkhu committed, friend? For what is this bhikkhu undergoing probation?’ They reply thus: ‘This bhikkhu, friend, committed two offenses entailing suspension, both concealed for two months—one offense concealed knowingly, the other concealed unknowingly. He asked the Saṅgha for two months’ probation for those offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted him two months’ probation for those offenses concealed for two months. These are the offenses this bhikkhu has committed, friend; for these he is undergoing probation.’ He then says, ‘The granting of probation for the offense that was concealed knowingly, friend, is lawful; it stands according to the Dhamma. But the granting of probation for the offense that was concealed unknowingly, friend, is unlawful; it does not stand according to the Dhamma. For one offense, friend, the bhikkhu is deserving of penance.’ ”

145. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekā āpatti saramānappaṭicchannā, ekā āpatti assaramānappaṭicchannā. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ deti. Tassa parivasantassa añño bhikkhu āgacchati bahussuto āgatāgamo dhammadharo vinayadharo mātikādharo paṇḍito viyatto medhāvī lajjī kukkuccako sikkhākāmo. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘ki ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno? Kissāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti? Te evaṃ vadenti – ‘ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekā āpatti saramānappaṭicchannā, ekā āpatti assaramānappaṭicchannā. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tāyo ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno; tāsāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘yāyaṃ, āvuso, āpatti saramānappaṭicchannā dhammikaṃ tassā āpattiyā parivāsadānaṃ; dhammattā ruhati. Yā ca khvāyaṃ, āvuso, āpatti assaramānappaṭicchannā, adhammikaṃ tassā āpattiyā parivāsadānaṃ; adhammattā na ruhati. Ekissā, āvuso, āpattiyā bhikkhu mānattāraho’’’ti.

145."Here, monks, a monk incurs two Saṅghādisesa offenses, both concealed for two months—one offense concealed while remembering, the other concealed while not remembering. He requests the Saṅgha for a two-month probation for those offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him a two-month probation for those offenses concealed for two months. While he is undergoing probation, another monk arrives—learned, versed in the tradition, a master of the Dhamma, a master of the Vinaya, a master of the summaries, wise, accomplished, intelligent, conscientious, scrupulous, and desirous of training. He asks, 'What offense has this monk incurred, friend? For what is this monk undergoing probation?' They reply, 'This monk, friend, incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses, both concealed for two months—one offense concealed while remembering, the other concealed while not remembering. He requested the Saṅgha for a two-month probation for those offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted him a two-month probation for those offenses concealed for two months. He has incurred these offenses, friend; for these he is undergoing probation.' He then says, 'The granting of probation for the offense that was concealed while remembering is lawful, friend; it is valid by the Dhamma. But the granting of probation for the offense that was concealed while not remembering is unlawful, friend; it is invalid by the Dhamma. For one offense, friend, the monk is deserving of penance.'"

146. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekā āpatti nibbematikappaṭicchannā, ekā āpatti vematikappaṭicchannā. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ deti. Tassa parivasantassa añño bhikkhu āgacchati bahussuto āgatāgamo dhammadharo vinayadharo mātikādharo paṇḍito viyatto medhāvī lajjī kukkuccako sikkhākāmo. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘kiṃ ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno? Kissāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti? Te evaṃ vadenti – ‘ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekā āpatti nibbematikappaṭicchannā, ekā āpatti vematikappaṭicchannā. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tāyo ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno; tāsāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘yāyaṃ, āvuso, āpatti nibbematikappaṭicchannā, dhammikaṃ tassā āpattiyā parivāsadānaṃ; dhammattā ruhati. Yā ca khvāyaṃ, āvuso, āpatti vematikappaṭicchannā adhammikaṃ tassā āpattiyā parivāsadānaṃ; adhammattā na ruhati. Ekissā, āvuso, āpattiyā bhikkhu mānattāraho’’ti.

146."Here, monks, a monk incurs two Saṅghādisesa offenses concealed for two months—one offense concealed with certainty, one offense concealed with uncertainty. He asks the Saṅgha for two months’ probation for those offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him two months’ probation for those offenses concealed for two months. While he is undergoing probation, another monk arrives—learned, versed in the tradition, a master of the Dhamma, a master of the Vinaya, a master of the summaries, wise, accomplished, intelligent, conscientious, scrupulous, and desirous of training. He says: ‘What offense has this monk incurred, friend? For what is this monk undergoing probation?’ They reply: ‘This monk, friend, incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses concealed for two months—one offense concealed with certainty, one offense concealed with uncertainty. He asked the Saṅgha for two months’ probation for those offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted him two months’ probation for those offenses concealed for two months. He incurred these offenses, friend; this is why he is undergoing probation.’ He says: ‘Friend, for the offense concealed with certainty, the granting of probation for that offense is legitimate; it is valid by the Dhamma. But for the offense concealed with uncertainty, the granting of probation for that offense is illegitimate; it is invalid by the Dhamma. Friend, for one offense the monk is worthy of penance.’"

147. Tena kho pana samayena aññattaro bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpanno hoti dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa etadahosi – ‘‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’’nti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami – ‘‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa me etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa me parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ [itarampi māsaparivāsaṃ (syā. ka. evamuparipi)] yāceyya’’nti.

147.Now at that time a certain monk had incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. Then it occurred to him: ‘I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Saṅgha for one month's probation for these two offenses concealed for two months?’ So he asked the Saṅgha for one month's probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted him one month's probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. While he was undergoing probation, a sense of shame arose in him: ‘I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. Then it occurred to me: "I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Saṅgha for one month's probation for these two offenses concealed for two months?" So I asked the Saṅgha for one month's probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted me one month's probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. While I was undergoing probation, a sense of shame arose in me. What if I were to ask the Saṅgha for an additional month's probation for these two offenses concealed for two months?’

So bhikkhūnaṃ ārocesi – ‘‘ahaṃ kho, āvuso, dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa me etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa me parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami – ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa me etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa me parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. Kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. ‘‘Tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho tassa bhikkhuno dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ detu. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, dātabbo –

The monk informed the other monks: "Friends, I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. Then it occurred to me: 'I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Saṅgha for one month of probation for these two offenses concealed for two months?' So I asked the Saṅgha for one month of probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted me one month of probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. While I was undergoing probation, a sense of shame arose in me: 'I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. Then it occurred to me: 'I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Saṅgha for one month of probation for these two offenses concealed for two months?' So I asked the Saṅgha for one month of probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted me one month of probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. While I was undergoing probation, a sense of shame arose in me. What if I were to ask the Saṅgha for an additional month of probation for these two offenses concealed for two months?' How should I proceed?" They reported the matter to the Blessed One. "In that case, monks, let the Saṅgha grant that monk an additional month of probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. And this is how it should be given:

‘‘Tena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā…pe… evamassa vacanīyo – ahaṃ, bhante, dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa me etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa me parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami – ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa me etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa me parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāceyyanti. Sohaṃ, bhante, saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācāmīti. Dutiyampi yācitabbo. Tatiyampi yācitabbo. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

"Therefore, monks, that monk should approach the Saṅgha... and he should say this: 'Venerable sirs, I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses concealed for two months. It occurred to me: "I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Saṅgha for one month’s probation for these two offenses concealed for two months?" So I asked the Saṅgha for one month’s probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted me one month’s probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. While I was undergoing probation, a sense of shame arose in me: "I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses concealed for two months. It occurred to me: 'I have incurred two Saṅghādisesa offenses concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Saṅgha for one month’s probation for these two offenses concealed for two months?' So I asked the Saṅgha for one month’s probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted me one month’s probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. While I was undergoing probation, a sense of shame arose in me. What if I were to ask the Saṅgha for an additional month’s probation for these two offenses concealed for two months?' Therefore, venerable sirs, I ask the Saṅgha for an additional month’s probation for these two offenses concealed for two months.' A second time it should be requested. A third time it should be requested. A competent and capable monk should inform the Saṅgha:

148. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami – ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa me etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa me parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāceyyanti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ dadeyya. Esā ñatti.

148."Venerable sir, may the Sangha listen to me. This monk named so-and-so committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. He thought: 'I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months?' He asked the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha granted him one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. While he was undergoing parivāsa, a sense of shame arose in him: 'I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months.' He thought: "I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months?" So I asked the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha granted me one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. While I was undergoing parivāsa, a sense of shame arose in me. What if I were to ask the Sangha for another month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months?' He now asks the Sangha for another month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. If the Sangha is ready, may the Sangha grant the monk named so-and-so another month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. This is the motion."

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami – ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa me etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa me parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācati. Saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ deti. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa bhikkhuno dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsassa [itarampi māsaparivāsassa (ka.), itarassapi māsaparivāsassa (syā.)] dānaṃ, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

"Venerable sir, may the Sangha listen to me. This monk named so-and-so committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. He thought: 'I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months?' So he asked the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha granted him one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. While he was undergoing parivāsa, a sense of shame arose in him: 'I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months.' He thought: "I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months?" So I asked the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha granted me one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. While I was undergoing parivāsa, a sense of shame arose in me. What if I were to ask the Sangha for another month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months?' So he asks the Sangha for another month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha grants the monk named so-and-so another month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. If the venerable ones approve of granting the monk named so-and-so another month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months, let them be silent. If anyone disapproves, let them speak."

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe….

"For the second time, I say this... For the third time, I say this..."

‘‘Dinno saṅghena itthannāmassa bhikkhuno dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāso [itarampi māsaparivāso (ka.), itaropi māsaparivāso (syā.)]. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

"The Sangha has granted the monk named so-and-so one further month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha approves; therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it."

‘‘Tena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā purimaṃ upādāya dve māsā parivasitabbā.

"Monks, that monk must then undergo parivāsa for two months, counting from the beginning."

149. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa evaṃ hoti – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ deti. Tassa parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami – ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Tassa me etadahosi – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ ekamāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tassa me parivasantassa lajjīdhammo okkami. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ deti. Tena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā purimaṃ upādāya dve māsā parivasitabbā.

149."Here, monks, a monk commits two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. He thinks: 'I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months?' He asks the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha grants him one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. While he is undergoing parivāsa, a sense of shame arose in him: 'I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. I thought: "I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. What if I were to ask the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months?" I asked the Sangha for one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha granted me one month of parivāsa for these two offenses concealed for two months. While I was undergoing parivāsa, a sense of shame arose in me. What if I were to ask the Sangha for parivāsa for another month for these two offenses concealed for two months?' He asks the Sangha for parivāsa for another month for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha grants him parivāsa for another month for these two offenses concealed for two months. That monk, monks, should undergo parivāsa for two months, counting from the first."

150. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekaṃ māsaṃ jānāti, ekaṃ māsaṃ na jānāti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ jānāti taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ jānāti taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto itarampi māsaṃ jānāti. Tassa evaṃ hoti – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekaṃ māsaṃ jāniṃ, ekaṃ māsaṃ na jāniṃ. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ jāniṃ taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ jāniṃ taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto itarampi māsaṃ jānāmi. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ deti. Tena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā purimaṃ upādāya dve māsā parivasitabbā.

150."Here, monks, a monk commits two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months; he knows of one month, but does not know of the other month. He asks the Sangha for parivāsa for the month he knows of, for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha grants him parivāsa for the month he knows of, for these two offenses concealed for two months. While on parivāsa, he comes to know of the other month as well. He thinks: 'I have committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months; I knew of one month, but did not know of the other month. I asked the Sangha for parivāsa for the month I knew of, for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha granted me parivāsa for the month I knew of, for these two offenses concealed for two months. While on parivāsa, I came to know of the other month as well. What if I were to ask the Sangha for parivāsa for the other month as well, for these two offenses concealed for two months?' He asks the Sangha for parivāsa for the other month as well, for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Sangha grants him parivāsa for the other month as well, for these two offenses concealed for two months. That monk, monks, should undergo parivāsa for two months, counting from the beginning."

151. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekaṃ māsaṃ sarati, ekaṃ māsaṃ nassarati. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ sarati taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ sarati taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto itarampi māsaṃ sarati. Tassa evaṃ hoti – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekaṃ māsaṃ sariṃ, ekaṃ māsaṃ nassariṃ. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ sariṃ taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ sariṃ taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto itarampi māsaṃ sarāmi. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ deti. Tena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā purimaṃ upādāya dve māsā parivasitabbā.

151."Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. He remembers one month, but does not remember the other month. He asks the Saṅgha for probation for the month he remembers, for the two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him probation for the month he remembers, for the two offenses concealed for two months. While on probation, he remembers the other month. He thinks: 'I committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. I remembered one month, but did not remember the other. I asked the Saṅgha for probation for the month I remembered, for the two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted me probation for the month I remembered, for the two offenses concealed for two months. While on probation, I remember the other month. Why not ask the Saṅgha for probation for the other month, for the two offenses concealed for two months?' He asks the Saṅgha for probation for the other month, for the two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him probation for the other month, for the two offenses concealed for two months. That bhikkhu, bhikkhus, should undergo two months of probation, counting from the first."

152. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekaṃ māsaṃ nibbematiko, ekaṃ māsaṃ vematiko. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ nibbematiko taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ nibbematiko taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto itarampi māsaṃ nibbematiko hoti. Tassa evaṃ hoti – ‘ahaṃ kho dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; ekaṃ māsaṃ nibbematiko, ekaṃ māsaṃ vematiko. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ nibbematiko taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchānnānaṃ yaṃ māsaṃ nibbematiko taṃ māsaṃ parivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto itarampi māsaṃ nibbematiko. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yāceyya’nti. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ itarampi māsaṃ parivāsaṃ deti. Tena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā purimaṃ upādāya dve māsā parivasitabbā.

152."Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. For one month he is without doubt, and for one month he is in doubt. He asks the Saṅgha for probation for the month he is without doubt, for the two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him probation for the month he is without doubt, for the two offenses concealed for two months. While on probation, he becomes without doubt about the other month as well. He thinks: 'I committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months. For one month I was without doubt, and for one month I was in doubt. I asked the Saṅgha for probation for the month I was without doubt, for the two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted me probation for the month I was without doubt, for the two offenses concealed for two months. While on probation, I became without doubt about the other month as well. Why not ask the Saṅgha for probation for the other month, for the two offenses concealed for two months?' He asks the Saṅgha for probation for the other month, for the two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him probation for the other month, for the two offenses concealed for two months. That bhikkhu, bhikkhus, should undergo two months of probation, counting from the first."

153. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; eko māso jānappaṭicchanno, eko māso ajānappaṭicchanno. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ deti. Tassa parivasantassa añño bhikkhu āgacchati bahussuto āgatāgamo dhammadharo vinayadharo mātikādharo paṇḍito viyatto medhāvī lajjī kukkuccako sikkhākāmo. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘kiṃ ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno? Kissāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti? Te evaṃ vadenti – ‘ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo. Eko māso jānappaṭicchanno, eko māso ajānappaṭicchanno. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tāyo ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno tāsāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘yvāyaṃ, āvuso, māso jānappaṭicchanno dhammikaṃ tassa māsassa parivāsadānaṃ; dhammattā ruhati. Yo ca khvāyaṃ, āvuso, māso ajānappaṭicchanno adhammikaṃ tassa māsassa parivāsadānaṃ; adhammattā na ruhati. Ekassa, āvuso, māsassa bhikkhu mānattāraho’ti.

153."Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months—one month knowingly concealed, one month unknowingly concealed. He asks the Saṅgha for two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. While he is on probation, another bhikkhu arrives—learned, versed in the tradition, a master of the Dhamma, a master of the Vinaya, a master of the Mātikā, wise, experienced, intelligent, conscientious, scrupulous, and desirous of training. He says: 'What offense has this bhikkhu committed, friend? Why is this bhikkhu undergoing probation?' They reply: 'Friend, this bhikkhu committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months—one month knowingly concealed, one month unknowingly concealed. He asked the Saṅgha for two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted him two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. These are the offenses he committed, and for these he is undergoing probation.' He says: 'Friend, that month which was knowingly concealed—the granting of probation for that month is legitimate; it is valid according to the Dhamma. But that month which was unknowingly concealed—the granting of probation for that month is illegitimate; it is invalid according to the Dhamma. For one month, friend, the bhikkhu is worthy of Mānatta.'"

154. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; eko māso saramānappaṭicchanno, eko māso assaramānappaṭicchanno. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ deti. Tassa parivasantassa añño bhikkhu āgacchati bahussuto āgatāgamo dhammadharo vinayadharo mātikādharo paṇḍito viyatto medhāvī lajjī kukkuccako sikkhākāmo. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘kiṃ ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno? Kissāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti? Te evaṃ vadenti – ‘ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; eko māso saramānappaṭicchanno, eko māso assaramānappaṭicchanno. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tāyo ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno tāsāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘yvāyaṃ, āvuso, māso saramānappaṭicchanno dhammikaṃ tassa māsassa parivāsadānaṃ; dhammattā ruhati. Yo ca khvāyaṃ, āvuso, māso assaramānappaṭicchanno adhammikaṃ tassa māsassa parivāsadānaṃ; adhammattā na ruhati. Ekassa, āvuso, māsassa bhikkhu mānattāraho’ti.

154."Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months—one month concealed with remembrance, one month concealed without remembrance. He asks the Saṅgha for two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. While he is undergoing probation, another bhikkhu arrives—learned, versed in the tradition, a master of the Dhamma, a master of the Vinaya, a master of the Mātikā, wise, experienced, intelligent, conscientious, scrupulous, and desirous of training. He says: 'What offense has this bhikkhu committed, friend? Why is this bhikkhu undergoing probation?' They reply: 'Friend, this bhikkhu committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months—one month concealed with remembrance, one month concealed without remembrance. He asked the Saṅgha for two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted him two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. These are the offenses he committed, and for these he is undergoing probation.' He says: 'Friend, that month which was concealed with remembrance—the granting of probation for that month is legitimate; it is valid according to the Dhamma. But that month which was concealed without remembrance—the granting of probation for that month is illegitimate; it is invalid according to the Dhamma. For one month, friend, the bhikkhu is worthy of Mānatta.'"

155. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; eko māso nibbematikappaṭicchanno, eko māso vematikappaṭicchanno. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ deti. Tassa parivasantassa añño bhikkhu āgacchati bahussuto āgatāgamo dhammadharo vinayadharo mātikādharo paṇḍito viyatto medhāvī lajjī kukkuccako sikkhākāmo. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘kiṃ ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno? Kissāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti? Te evaṃ vadenti – ‘ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu dve saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji dvemāsappaṭicchannāyo; eko māso nibbematikappaṭicchanno, eko māso vematikappaṭicchanno. So saṅghaṃ dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ yāci. Tassa saṅgho dvinnaṃ āpattīnaṃ dvemāsappaṭicchannānaṃ dvemāsaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Tāyo ayaṃ, āvuso, bhikkhu āpanno tāsāyaṃ bhikkhu parivasatī’ti. So evaṃ vadeti – ‘yvāyaṃ, āvuso, māso nibbematikappaṭicchanno dhammikaṃ tassa māsassa parivāsadānaṃ; dhammattā ruhati. Yo ca khvāyaṃ, āvuso, māso vematikappaṭicchanno adhammikaṃ tassa māsassa parivāsadānaṃ; adhammattā na ruhati. Ekassa, āvuso, māsassa bhikkhu mānattāraho’’ti.

155."Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months—one month concealed without doubt, one month concealed with doubt. He asks the Saṅgha for two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha grants him two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. While he is undergoing probation, another bhikkhu arrives—learned, versed in the tradition, a master of the Dhamma, a master of the Vinaya, a master of the Mātikā, wise, experienced, intelligent, conscientious, scrupulous, and desirous of training. He asks: 'What offense has this bhikkhu committed, friend? For what is this bhikkhu undergoing probation?' They reply: 'Friend, this bhikkhu has committed two Saṅghādisesa offenses, concealed for two months—one month concealed without doubt, one month concealed with doubt. He asked the Saṅgha for two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. The Saṅgha granted him two months' probation for these two offenses concealed for two months. These are the offenses he has committed, and for these he is undergoing probation.' He then says: 'Friend, that month which was concealed without doubt—the granting of probation for that month is legitimate; it is valid according to the Dhamma. But that month which was concealed with doubt—the granting of probation for that month is illegitimate; it is invalid according to the Dhamma. For one month, friend, the bhikkhu is worthy of Mānatta.'"

Suddhantaparivāso

Probation for an Indeterminate Period

156. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpanno hoti. So āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. So bhikkhūnaṃ ārocesi – ‘‘ahaṃ, āvuso, sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ; āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāmi, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāmi; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarāmi, rattipariyantaṃ nassarāmi; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. Kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabba’’nti? Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. ‘‘Tena hi, bhikkhave, saṅgho tassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ detu. Evañca pana, bhikkhave, dātabbo –

156.At that time, a certain bhikkhu had committed several Saṅghādisesa offenses. He did not know the extent of the offenses, nor did he know the number of nights; he did not remember the extent of the offenses, nor did he remember the number of nights; he was uncertain about the extent of the offenses, and uncertain about the number of nights. He informed the bhikkhus, 'Friends, I have committed several Saṅghādisesa offenses. I do not know the extent of the offenses, nor do I know the number of nights; I do not remember the extent of the offenses, nor do I remember the number of nights; I am uncertain about the extent of the offenses, and uncertain about the number of nights. How should I proceed?' They reported the matter to the Blessed One. 'In that case, bhikkhus, let the Saṅgha grant that bhikkhu probation for an indeterminate period for those offenses. And thus, bhikkhus, it should be granted:

‘‘Tena, bhikkhave, bhikkhunā saṅghaṃ upasaṅkamitvā…pe… evamassa vacanīyo – ‘ahaṃ, bhante, sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ. Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāmi, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāmi; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarāmi, rattipariyantaṃ nassarāmi; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. Sohaṃ, bhante, saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ yācāmī’ti. Dutiyampi yācitabbo. Tatiyampi yācitabbo. Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṅgho ñāpetabbo –

That bhikkhu, bhikkhus, should approach the Saṅgha [...] and say, 'Venerable sirs, I have committed several Saṅghādisesa offenses. I do not know the extent of the offenses, nor do I know the number of nights; I do not remember the extent of the offenses, nor do I remember the number of nights; I am uncertain about the extent of the offenses, and uncertain about the number of nights. Therefore, venerable sirs, I request the Saṅgha for probation for an indeterminate period for those offenses.' He should be asked a second time. He should be asked a third time. A competent and capable bhikkhu should inform the Saṅgha:

157. ‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji. Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ yācati. Yadi saṅghassa pattakallaṃ, saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ dadeyya. Esā ñatti.

157.Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha listen to me. This bhikkhu named so-and-so has committed several Saṅghādisesa offenses. He does not know the extent of the offenses, nor does he know the number of nights; he does not remember the extent of the offenses, nor does he remember the number of nights; he is uncertain about the extent of the offenses, and uncertain about the number of nights. He requests the Saṅgha for probation for an indeterminate period for those offenses. If the Saṅgha is ready, may the Saṅgha grant the bhikkhu named so-and-so probation for an indeterminate period for those offenses. This is the motion.

‘‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṅgho. Ayaṃ itthannāmo bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajji. Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ yācati. Saṅgho itthannāmassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsaṃ deti. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāsassa dānaṃ, so tuṇhassa; yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya.

Venerable sirs, may the Saṅgha hear me. This bhikkhu, named so-and-so, has committed several Saṅghādisesa offenses. He does not know the extent of the offenses, nor does he know the number of nights; he does not remember the extent of the offenses, nor does he remember the number of nights; he is uncertain about the extent of the offenses, and uncertain about the number of nights. He requests the Saṅgha for probation for an indeterminate period for these offenses. The Saṅgha grants the bhikkhu, named so-and-so, probation for an indeterminate period for these offenses. Any venerable one who approves of granting probation for an indeterminate period for these offenses to the bhikkhu named so-and-so, let him be silent; any who does not approve, let him speak.

‘‘Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe… tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi…pe….

For the second time, I say this [...]; for the third time, I say this [...].

‘‘Dinno saṅghena itthannāmassa bhikkhuno tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ suddhantaparivāso. Khamati saṅghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’’ti.

Probation for an indeterminate period for these offenses has been granted by the Saṅgha to the bhikkhu named so-and-so. It is approved by the Saṅgha, therefore it is silent. Thus I hold it.

158. ‘‘Evaṃ kho, bhikkhave, suddhantaparivāso dātabbo; evaṃ parivāso dātabbo. Kathañca, bhikkhave, suddhantaparivāso dātabbo? Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante vematiko – suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

158.Thus, bhikkhus, probation for an indeterminate period should be granted; thus should probation be granted. And how, bhikkhus, should probation for an indeterminate period be granted? He does not know the extent of the offenses, nor does he know the number of nights; he does not remember the extent of the offenses, nor does he remember the number of nights; he is uncertain about the extent of the offenses, and uncertain about the number of nights—probation for an indeterminate period should be granted.

‘‘Āpattipariyantaṃ jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ sarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; āpattipariyante nibbematiko, rattipariyante vematiko – suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

He knows the extent of the offenses but does not know the number of nights; he remembers the extent of the offenses but does not remember the number of nights; he is certain about the extent of the offenses but is uncertain about the number of nights—probation for an indeterminate period should be granted.

‘‘Āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ na jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ nassarati; āpattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko, rattipariyante vematiko – suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

He knows some of the extent of the offenses but not others, and does not know the number of nights; he remembers some of the extent of the offenses but not others, and does not remember the number of nights; he is uncertain about some of the extent of the offenses but certain about others, and uncertain about the number of nights—probation for an indeterminate period should be granted.

‘‘Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati; āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko – suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

He does not know the extent of the offenses, but knows the number of nights in some instances and does not in others; he does not remember the extent of the offenses, but remembers the number of nights in some instances and does not in others; he is uncertain about the extent of the offenses, but is uncertain about the number of nights in some instances and certain in others—probation for an indeterminate period should be granted.

‘‘Āpattipariyantaṃ jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ sarati, rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati; āpattipariyante nibbematiko, rattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko – suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

He knows the extent of the offenses, and knows some of the number of nights but not others; he remembers the extent of the offenses, and remembers some of the number of nights but not others; he is certain about the extent of the offenses, but uncertain about some of the number of nights and certain about others—probation for an indeterminate period should be granted.

‘‘Āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti; rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati; rattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati; āpattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko; rattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko – suddhantaparivāso dātabbo. Evaṃ kho, bhikkhave, suddhantaparivāso dātabbo.

He knows some of the extent of the offenses but not others; he knows some of the number of nights but not others; he remembers some of the extent of the offenses but not others; he remembers some of the number of nights but not others; he is uncertain about some of the extent of the offenses but certain about others; he is uncertain about some of the number of nights but certain about others—probation for an indeterminate period should be granted. Thus, bhikkhus, probation for an indeterminate period should be granted.

159. ‘‘Kathañca, bhikkhave, parivāso dātabbo? Āpattipariyantaṃ jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ sarati, rattipariyantaṃ sarati; āpattipariyante nibbematiko, rattipariyante nibbematiko – parivāso dātabbo.

159.And how, bhikkhus, should probation be granted? He knows the extent of the offenses, he knows the number of nights; he remembers the extent of the offenses, he remembers the number of nights; he is certain about the extent of the offenses, he is certain about the number of nights—probation should be granted.

‘‘Āpattipariyantaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ sarati, āpattipariyante vematiko, rattipariyante nibbematiko – parivāso dātabbo.

He does not know the extent of the offenses, but he knows the number of nights; he does not remember the extent of the offenses, but he remembers the number of nights; he is uncertain about the extent of the offenses, but he is certain about the number of nights—probation should be granted.

‘‘Āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ jānāti, ekaccaṃ na jānāti, rattipariyantaṃ jānāti; āpattipariyantaṃ ekaccaṃ sarati, ekaccaṃ nassarati, rattipariyantaṃ sarati; āpattipariyante ekacce vematiko, ekacce nibbematiko, rattipariyante nibbematiko – parivāso dātabbo. Evaṃ kho, bhikkhave, parivāso dātabbo.

He knows some of the extent of the offenses but not others, but knows the number of nights; he remembers some of the extent of the offenses but not others, but remembers the number of nights; he is uncertain about some of the extent of the offenses but certain about others, and is certain about the number of nights—probation should be granted. Thus, bhikkhus, probation should be granted.

Parivāso niṭṭhito.

The probation is concluded.

### 3. Cattālīsakaṃ ^3

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv13-brahmali-pali#^3|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV13.3" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


3.The Forty

160. Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu parivasanto vibbhami. So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yāci. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ.

160.At that time a certain bhikkhu, while undergoing probation, became disaffected. He then returned and requested higher ordination from the bhikkhus. They reported the matter to the Blessed One.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto vibbhamati. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing probation becomes disaffected. For one who has become disaffected, bhikkhus, the probation does not count. If he is reordained, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto sāmaṇero hoti. Sāmaṇerassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing probation becomes a novice. For a novice, bhikkhus, the probation does not count. If he is reordained, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto ummattako hoti. Ummattakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. So ce puna anummattako hoti, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing probation becomes insane. For an insane person, bhikkhus, the probation does not count. If he later becomes sane, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto khittacitto hoti. Khittacittassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. So ce puna akhittacitto hoti, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo purivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing probation becomes deranged in mind. For one who is deranged in mind, bhikkhus, the probation does not count. If he later becomes underranged in mind, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto vedanāṭṭo hoti. Vedanāṭṭassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. So ce puna avedanāṭṭo hoti, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing probation is afflicted by pain. For one afflicted by pain, bhikkhus, the probation does not count. If he later is not afflicted by pain, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto, āpattiyā adassane, ukkhipiyyati [ukkhipiyati (syā.), ukkhipīyati (ka.)]. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. So ce puna osāriyyati [osāriyati (syā.), osārīyati (ka.)], tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing probation is suspended for not acknowledging an offense. For one who is suspended, bhikkhus, the probation does not count. If he is later reinstated, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto, āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhipiyyati. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing probation is suspended for not making amends for an offense. For one who is suspended, bhikkhus, the probation does not count. If he is later reinstated, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto, pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, parivāso na ruhati. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho, avaseso parivasitabbo.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing probation is suspended for not relinquishing a wrong view. For one who is suspended, bhikkhus, the probation does not count. If he is later reinstated, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

161. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mūlāyapaṭikassanāraho vibbhamati. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, mūlāyapaṭikassanā na ruhati. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo.

161.Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu deserving of being sent back to the beginning becomes disaffected. For one who has become disaffected, bhikkhus, the sending back to the beginning does not count. If he is reordained, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone. That bhikkhu must be sent back to the beginning.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mūlāyapaṭikassanāraho sāmaṇero hoti…pe… ummattako hoti…pe… khittacitto hoti…pe… vedanāṭṭo hoti…pe… āpattiyā adassane ukkhipiyyati…pe… āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhipiyyati…pe… pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, mūlāyapaṭikassanā na ruhati. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu deserving of being sent back to the beginning becomes a novice… becomes insane… becomes deranged in mind… is afflicted by pain… is suspended for not acknowledging an offense… is suspended for not making amends for an offense… is suspended for not relinquishing a wrong view. For one who is suspended, bhikkhus, the sending back to the beginning does not count. If he is later reinstated, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone. That bhikkhu must be sent back to the beginning.

162. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattāraho vibbhamati. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, mānattadānaṃ na ruhati. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho. Tassa bhikkhuno mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

162.Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu deserving of penance becomes disaffected. For one who has become disaffected, bhikkhus, the grant of penance does not count. If he is reordained, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone. That bhikkhu must be given the penance.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattāraho sāmaṇero hoti…pe… ummattako hoti…pe… khittacitto hoti…pe… vedanāṭṭo hoti…pe… āpattiyā adassane, ukkhipiyyati…pe… āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhipiyyati…pe… pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, mānattadānaṃ na ruhati. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho. Tassa bhikkhuno mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu deserving of penance becomes a novice… becomes insane… becomes deranged in mind… is afflicted by pain… is suspended for not acknowledging an offense… is suspended for not making amends for an offense… is suspended for not relinquishing a wrong view. For one who is suspended, bhikkhus, the grant of penance does not count. If he is later reinstated, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone. That bhikkhu must be given the penance.

163. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattaṃ caranto vibbhamati. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, mānattacariyā na ruhati. So ce puna upasampajjati tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho; yaṃ mānattaṃ dinnaṃ sudinnaṃ, yaṃ mānattaṃ ciṇṇaṃ suciṇṇaṃ, avasesaṃ caritabbaṃ.

163.Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing penance becomes disaffected. For one who has become disaffected, bhikkhus, the performance of penance does not count. If he is reordained, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the penance that was granted was well granted, the penance that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattaṃ caranto sāmaṇero hoti…pe… ummattako hoti…pe… khittacitto hoti…pe… vedanāṭṭo hoti…pe… āpattiyā adassane, ukkhipiyyati…pe… āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhipiyyati…pe… pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, mānattacariyā na ruhati. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo purivuttho suparivuttho; yaṃ mānattaṃ dinnaṃ sudinnaṃ, yaṃ mānattaṃ ciṇṇaṃ suciṇṇaṃ, avasesaṃ caritabbaṃ.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu undergoing penance becomes a novice… becomes insane… becomes deranged in mind… is afflicted by pain… is suspended for not acknowledging an offense… is suspended for not making amends for an offense… is suspended for not relinquishing a wrong view. For one who is suspended, bhikkhus, the performance of penance does not count. If he is later reinstated, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the penance that was granted was well granted, the penance that was undergone was well undergone; the remainder must be undergone.

164. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu abbhānāraho vibbhamati. Vibbhantakassa, bhikkhave, abbhānaṃ na ruhati. So ce puna upasampajjati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho; yaṃ mānattaṃ dinnaṃ sudinnaṃ, yaṃ mānattaṃ ciṇṇaṃ suciṇṇaṃ. So bhikkhu abbhetabbo.

164.Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu deserving of rehabilitation becomes disaffected. For one who has become disaffected, bhikkhus, the rehabilitation does not count. If he is reordained, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the penance that was granted was well granted, the penance that was undergone was well undergone. That bhikkhu must be rehabilitated.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu abbhānāraho sāmaṇero hoti…pe… ummattako hoti…pe…

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu deserving of rehabilitation becomes a novice… becomes insane…

Khittacitto hoti…pe… vedanāṭṭo hoti…pe… āpattiyā adassane, ukkhipiyyati…pe… āpattiyā appaṭikamme, ukkhipiyyati…pe… pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā, appaṭinissagge, ukkhipiyyati. Ukkhittakassa, bhikkhave, abbhānaṃ na ruhati. So ce puna osāriyyati, tassa tadeva purimaṃ parivāsadānaṃ. Yo parivāso dinno sudinno, yo parivuttho suparivuttho; yaṃ mānattaṃ dinnaṃ sudinnaṃ, yaṃ mānattaṃ ciṇṇaṃ suciṇṇaṃ. So bhikkhu abbhetabbo.

becomes deranged in mind… is afflicted by pain… is suspended for not acknowledging an offense… is suspended for not making amends for an offense… is suspended for not relinquishing a wrong view. For one who is suspended, bhikkhus, the rehabilitation does not count. If he is later reinstated, that previous grant of probation remains valid. The probation that was given was well given, the probation that was undergone was well undergone; the penance that was granted was well granted, the penance that was undergone was well undergone. That bhikkhu must be rehabilitated.

Cattālīsakaṃ samattaṃ.

The Forty: Concluded.

### 4. Chattiṃsakaṃ ^4

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv13-brahmali-pali#^4|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>
