> "VIN-CV13.6" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


6.Four hundred cases of combined probation including reversion to the beginning.

172. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo.

172.Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses without concealing them, and then falls away. Having been reordained again, he does not conceal those offenses. That monk should be reverted to the beginning.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses without concealing them, and then falls away. Having been reordained again, he conceals those offenses. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā paṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses, having concealed them, and then falls away. Having been reordained again, he does not conceal those offenses. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā paṭicchādetvā vibbhamati. So puna upasampanno tā āpattiyo chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses, having concealed them, and then falls away. Having been reordained again, he conceals those offenses. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

173. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

173.Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some of his offenses are concealed and some are unconcealed. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously concealed, he does not conceal afterward; the offenses he previously did not conceal, he does not conceal afterward. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some of his offenses are concealed and some are unconcealed. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously concealed, he does not conceal afterward; the offenses he previously did not conceal, he conceals afterward. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some of his offenses are concealed and some are unconcealed. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously concealed, he conceals afterward; the offenses he previously did not conceal, he does not conceal afterward. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some of his offenses are concealed and some are unconcealed. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously concealed, he conceals afterward; the offenses he previously did not conceal, he conceals afterward. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

174. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti. Yā āpattiyo jānāti tā āpattiyo chādeti; yā āpattiyo na jānāti tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe jānitvā chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe ajānitvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

174.Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some offenses he knows, some offenses he does not know. The offenses he knows, he conceals; the offenses he does not know, he does not conceal. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously knew and concealed, he later knows and does not conceal; the offenses he previously did not know and did not conceal, he later knows and does not conceal. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti. Yā āpattiyo jānāti tā āpattiyo chādeti; yā āpattiyo na jānāti tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe jānitvā chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe ajānitvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some offenses he knows, some offenses he does not know. The offenses he knows, he conceals; the offenses he does not know, he does not conceal. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously knew and concealed, he later knows and does not conceal; the offenses he previously did not know and did not conceal, he later knows and conceals. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti. Yā āpattiyo jānāti tā āpattiyo chādeti; yā āpattiyo na jānāti tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe jānitvā chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe ajānitvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some offenses he knows, some offenses he does not know. The offenses he knows, he conceals; the offenses he does not know, he does not conceal. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously knew and concealed, he later knows and conceals; the offenses he previously did not know and did not conceal, he later knows and does not conceal. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti. Yā āpattiyo jānāti tā āpattiyo chādeti, yā āpattiyo na jānāti tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe jānitvā chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe ajānitvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā jānitvā chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some offenses he knows, some offenses he does not know. The offenses he knows, he conceals; the offenses he does not know, he does not conceal. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously knew and concealed, he later knows and conceals; the offenses he previously did not know and did not conceal, he later knows and conceals. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

175. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccā āpattiyo sarati, ekaccā āpattiyo nassarati. Yā āpattiyo sarati tā āpattiyo chādeti; yā āpattiyo nassarati tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe saritvā chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā saritvā nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe assaritvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā saritvā nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

175.Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some offenses he remembers, some offenses he does not remember. The offenses he remembers, he conceals; the offenses he does not remember, he does not conceal. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously remembered and concealed, he later remembers and does not conceal; the offenses he previously did not remember and did not conceal, he later remembers and does not conceal. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccā āpattiyo sarati, ekaccā āpattiyo nassarati. Yā āpattiyo sarati tā āpattiyo chādeti; yā āpattiyo nassarati tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe saritvā chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā saritvā nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe assaritvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā saritvā chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation meanwhile commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. Some offenses he remembers, some offenses he does not remember. The offenses he remembers, he conceals; the offenses he does not remember, he does not conceal. Having fallen away, and having been reordained again, the offenses he previously remembered and concealed, he later remembers and does not conceal; the offenses he previously did not remember and did not conceal, he later remembers and conceals. That monk should be reverted to the beginning. And for those offenses that were concealed, combined probation should be given, reckoning from the earliest offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccā āpattiyo sarati, ekaccā āpattiyo nassarati. Yā āpattiyo sarati tā āpattiyo chādeti; yā āpattiyo nassarati tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe saritvā chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā saritvā chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe assaritvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā saritvā nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. He remembers some offenses, and he does not remember others. Those offenses he remembers, he conceals; those offenses he does not remember, he does not conceal. Having lapsed and been reordained, those offenses he previously remembered and concealed, he later remembers and conceals; those offenses he previously did not remember and did not conceal, he later remembers and does not conceal. That monk should be drawn back to the root. And for his concealed offenses, a concurrent probation should be given, counting from the first offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccā āpattiyo sarati, ekaccā āpattiyo nassarati. Yā āpattiyo sarati tā āpattiyo chādeti; yā āpattiyo nassarati tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe saritvā chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā saritvā chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe assaritvā nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā saritvā chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. He remembers some offenses, and he does not remember others. Those offenses he remembers, he conceals; those offenses he does not remember, he does not conceal. Having lapsed and been reordained, those offenses he previously remembered and concealed, he later remembers and conceals; those offenses he previously did not remember and did not conceal, he later remembers and does not conceal. That monk should be drawn back to the root. And for his concealed offenses, a concurrent probation should be given, counting from the first offense.

176. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. Yāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko tā āpattiyo chādeti; yāsu āpattīsu vematiko tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

176.Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses. About some offenses he is certain, about others he is uncertain. Those offenses about which he is certain, he conceals; those offenses about which he is uncertain, he does not conceal. Having lapsed and been reordained, those offenses he was previously certain about and concealed, he later is certain about and does not conceal; those offenses he was previously uncertain about and did not conceal, he later is certain about and does not conceal. That monk should be drawn back to the root. And for his concealed offenses, a concurrent probation should be given, counting from the first offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. Yāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko tā āpattiyo chādeti; yāsu āpattīsu vematiko tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses in the interval. About some offenses he is certain, about others he is doubtful. Those offenses he is certain about, he conceals; those offenses he is doubtful about, he does not conceal. Having lapsed and been reordained, those offenses he was previously certain about and concealed, he later is certain about and does not conceal; those offenses he was previously doubtful about and did not conceal, he later is certain about and conceals. That monk should be drawn back to the root. And for his concealed offenses, a concurrent probation should be given, counting from the first offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. Yāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko tā āpattiyo chādeti; yāsu āpattīsu vematiko tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses in the interval. About some offenses he is certain, about others he is uncertain. Those offenses about which he is certain, he conceals; those offenses about which he is uncertain, he does not conceal. Having lapsed and been reordained, those offenses he was previously certain about and concealed, he later is certain about and conceals; those offenses he was previously uncertain about and did not conceal, he later is certain about and does not conceal. That monk should be drawn back to the root. And for his concealed offenses, a concurrent probation should be given, counting from the first offense.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati. Ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. Yāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko tā āpattiyo chādeti; yāsu āpattīsu vematiko tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vibbhamitvā [so bhikkhu vibbhamitvā (ka.)] puna upasampanno yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses in the interval. About some offenses he is certain, about others he is doubtful. Those offenses he is certain about, he conceals; those offenses he is doubtful about, he does not conceal. Having lapsed and been reordained, those offenses he was previously certain about and concealed, he later is certain about and conceals; those offenses he was previously doubtful about and did not conceal, he later is certain about and conceals. That monk should be drawn back to the root. And for his concealed offenses, a concurrent probation should be given, counting from the first offense.

177. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā sāmaṇero hoti…pe… ummattako hoti…pe… khittacitto hoti…pe… vedanāṭṭo hoti…pe… tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi (yathā heṭṭhā vitthāritaṃ tathā vitthāretabbaṃ)…pe… ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti…pe… ekaccā āpattiyo sarati, ekaccā āpattiyo nassarati…pe… ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. Yāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko tā āpattiyo chādeti; yāsu āpattīsu vematiko tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vedanāṭṭo hoti. So puna avedanāṭṭo hutvā yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti…pe… yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti…pe… yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti…pe… yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

177.Here, monks, a monk undergoing probation commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses in the interval, without concealing them, and becomes a novice… or becomes insane… or becomes mentally deranged… or becomes afflicted with pain… His offenses may be concealed or unconcealed (as explained in detail below)… He knows some offenses but not others… He remembers some offenses but not others… About some offenses he is certain, about others he is doubtful. Those offenses he is certain about, he conceals; those offenses he is doubtful about, he does not conceal. He is afflicted with pain. Later, when he is no longer afflicted with pain, those offenses he was previously certain about and concealed, he later is certain about and does not conceal; those offenses he was previously doubtful about and did not conceal, he later is certain about and does not conceal… Or those offenses he was previously certain about and concealed, he later is certain about and does not conceal; those offenses he was previously doubtful about and did not conceal, he later is certain about and conceals… Or those offenses he was previously certain about and concealed, he later is certain about and conceals; those offenses he was previously doubtful about and did not conceal, he later is certain about and does not conceal… Or those offenses he was previously certain about and concealed, he later is certain about and conceals; those offenses he was previously doubtful about and did not conceal, he later is certain about and conceals. That monk should be drawn back to the root. And for his concealed offenses, a concurrent probation should be given, counting from the first offense.

178. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu mānattāraho…pe… mānattaṃ caranto…pe… abbhānāraho antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati…pe… (mānattāraho ca mānattacārī ca abbhānāraho ca yathā parivāso vitthārito tathā vitthāretabbo).

178.Here, monks, a monk deserving penance… or while undergoing penance… or deserving reinstatement commits several Saṅghādisesa offenses in the interval, without concealing them, and lapses… (The cases of one deserving penance, undergoing penance, and deserving reinstatement should be explained in detail as with probation).

179. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu abbhānāraho antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā appaṭicchādetvā sāmaṇero hoti…pe… ummattako hoti…pe… khittacitto hoti…pe… vedanāṭṭo hoti…pe… tassa honti āpattiyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi …pe… ekaccā āpattiyo jānāti, ekaccā āpattiyo na jānāti…pe… ekaccā āpattiyo sarati, ekaccā āpattiyo nassarati…pe… ekaccāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko, ekaccāsu āpattīsu vematiko. Yāsu āpattīsu nibbematiko tā āpattiyo chādeti; yāsu āpattīsu vematiko tā āpattiyo nacchādeti. So vedanāṭṭo hoti. So puna avedanāṭṭo hutvā yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti…pe… yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti…pe… yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko nacchādeti…pe… yā āpattiyo pubbe nibbematiko chādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti; yā āpattiyo pubbe vematiko nacchādesi tā āpattiyo pacchā nibbematiko chādeti. So bhikkhu mūlāya paṭikassitabbo. Yathāpaṭicchannānañcassa āpattīnaṃ purimāya āpattiyā samodhānaparivāso dātabbo.

179.Here, monks, a monk liable to suspension, having incurred many Saṅghādisesa offenses in the interim without concealing them, becomes a novice… or becomes insane… or becomes deranged in mind… or is afflicted with pain… Some of his offenses are concealed, some are not concealed… He knows some offenses, he does not know some offenses… He remembers some offenses, he does not remember some offenses… He is certain about some offenses, he is uncertain about some offenses. The offenses about which he is certain, he conceals; the offenses about which he is uncertain, he does not conceal. He is afflicted with pain. Then, when he is no longer afflicted with pain, the offenses that he was previously certain about and concealed, he is later certain about and does not conceal; the offenses that he was previously uncertain about and did not conceal, he is later certain about and does not conceal… The offenses that he was previously certain about and concealed, he is later certain about and conceals; the offenses that he was previously uncertain about and did not conceal, he is later certain about and conceals. That monk must be relegated to the beginning. And for his concealed offenses, a probation of combination with the first offense should be given.

Samūlāyasamodhānaparivāsacatussataṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The four hundred cases of probation of combination with root-relegation are concluded.

### 7. Parimāṇādivāraaṭṭhakaṃ ^7

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv13-brahmali-pali#^7|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV13.7" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


7.The eightfold section beginning with measure.

180. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjitvā parimāṇā appaṭicchādetvā…pe… aparimāṇā appaṭicchādetvā…pe… ekanāmā appaṭicchādetvā…pe… nānānāmā appaṭicchādetvā…pe… sabhāgā appaṭicchādetvā…pe… visabhāgā appaṭicchādetvā…pe… vavatthitā appaṭicchādetvā…pe… sambhinnā appaṭicchādetvā vibbhamati…pe… (yathā heṭṭhā tathā vitthāretabbaṃ).

180.“Here, monks, a monk, having incurred many Saṅghādisesa offenses, without concealing a limited number… without concealing an unlimited number… without concealing those of a single type… without concealing those of diverse types… without concealing those that are similar… without concealing those that are dissimilar… without concealing those that are determined… without concealing those that are mixed, goes astray… (to be elaborated as above).”

Parimāṇādivāraaṭṭhakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The eightfold section beginning with measure is concluded.

### 8. Dvebhikkhuvāraekādasakaṃ ^8

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv13-brahmali-pali#^8|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV13.8" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


8.The eleventh section on two monks.

181. ‘‘Dve bhikkhū saṅghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Te saṅghādisese saṅghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Yathāpaṭicchanne [yathāpaṭicchannānaṃ (sī.)] cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

181.“Two monks have incurred a Saṅghādisesa offense. They are of the view that it is a Saṅghādisesa. One conceals it, the other does not conceal it. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. After giving him probation corresponding to the period concealed, both should be given mānatta.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū saṅghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Te saṅghādisese vematikā honti. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

“Two monks have incurred a Saṅghādisesa offense. They are uncertain about the Saṅghādisesa. One conceals it, the other does not conceal it. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. After giving him probation corresponding to the period concealed, both should be given mānatta.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū saṅghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Te saṅghādisese missakadiṭṭhino honti. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

“Two monks have incurred a Saṅghādisesa offense. They are of mixed views regarding the Saṅghādisesa. One conceals it, the other does not conceal it. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. After giving him probation corresponding to the period concealed, both should be given mānatta.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū missakaṃ āpannā honti. Te missake saṅghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

“Two monks have incurred a mixed offense. They are of the view that the mixed offense is a Saṅghādisesa. One conceals it, the other does not conceal it. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. After giving him probation corresponding to the period concealed, both should be given mānatta.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū missakaṃ āpannā honti. Te missake missakadiṭṭhino honti. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

“Two monks have incurred a mixed offense. They are of the view that the mixed offense is a mixed offense. One conceals it, the other does not conceal it. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. After giving him probation corresponding to the period concealed, both should be given mānatta.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū suddhakaṃ āpannā honti. Te suddhake saṅghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Ubhopi yathādhammaṃ kārāpetabbā.

“Two monks have incurred a pure offense. They are of the view that the pure offense is a Saṅghādisesa. One conceals it, the other does not conceal it. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. Both should be dealt with according to the Dhamma.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū suddhakaṃ āpannā honti. Te suddhake suddhakadiṭṭhino honti. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Ubhopi yathādhammaṃ kārāpetabbā.

“Two monks have incurred a pure offense. They are of the view that the pure offense is a pure offense. One conceals it, the other does not conceal it. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. Both should be dealt with according to the Dhamma.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū saṅghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Te saṅghādisese saṅghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. Ekassa hoti ārocessāmīti, ekassa hoti na ārocessāmīti. So paṭhamampi yāmaṃ chādeti, dutiyampi yāmaṃ chādeti, tatiyampi yāmaṃ chādeti – uṭṭhite aruṇe channā hoti āpatti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

“Two monks have incurred a Saṅghādisesa offense. They are of the view that the Saṅghādisesa is a Saṅghādisesa. One thinks, ‘I will declare it,’ the other thinks, ‘I will not declare it.’ He conceals it during the first watch, conceals it during the second watch, and conceals it during the third watch. When dawn rises, the offense is concealed. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. After giving him probation corresponding to the period concealed, both should be given mānatta.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū saṅghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Te saṅghādisese saṅghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. Te gacchanti ārocessāmāti. Ekassa antarāmagge makkhadhammo uppajjati na ārocessāmīti. So paṭhamampi yāmaṃ chādeti, dutiyampi yāmaṃ chādeti, tatiyampi yāmaṃ chādeti – uṭṭhite aruṇe channā hoti āpatti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

“Two monks have incurred a Saṅghādisesa offense. They are of the view that the Saṅghādisesa is a Saṅghādisesa. They go, thinking, ‘We will declare it.’ On the way, a disposition to dissemble arises in one: ‘I will not declare it.’ He conceals it during the first watch, he conceals it during the second watch, he conceals it during the third watch—when dawn rises, the offense is concealed. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. After giving him probation corresponding to the period concealed, both should be given mānatta.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū saṅghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Te saṅghādisese saṅghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. Te ummattakā honti. Te pacchā anummattakā hutvā eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

“Two monks have incurred a Saṅghādisesa offense. They are of the view that the Saṅghādisesa is a Saṅghādisesa. They are insane. Later, having recovered their sanity, one conceals it, the other does not conceal it. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. After giving him probation corresponding to the period concealed, both should be given mānatta.”

‘‘Dve bhikkhū saṅghādisesaṃ āpannā honti. Te pātimokkhe uddissamāne evaṃ vadanti – ‘idāneva kho mayaṃ jānāma – ayampi kira dhammo suttāgato suttapariyāpanno anvaddhamāsaṃ uddesaṃ āgacchatī’ti. Te saṅghādisese saṅghādisesadiṭṭhino honti. Eko chādeti, eko nacchādeti. Yo chādeti so dukkaṭaṃ desāpetabbo. Yathāpaṭicchanne cassa parivāsaṃ datvā ubhinnampi mānattaṃ dātabbaṃ.

“Two monks have incurred a Saṅghādisesa offense. While the Pātimokkha is being recited, they say: ‘Only now do we know that this rule, it seems, is included in the Suttas and is recited every half-month.’ They are of the view that the Saṅghādisesa is a Saṅghādisesa. One conceals it, one does not conceal it. The one who conceals it should be made to confess a dukkaṭa offense. After giving him probation corresponding to the period concealed, both should be given mānatta.”

Dvebhikkhuvāraekādasakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The eleventh section on two monks is concluded.

### 9. Mūlāyaavisuddhinavakaṃ ^9

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv13-brahmali-pali#^9|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV13.9" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


9.The Ninefold Section on Impurity Concerning the Root.

182. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi.

182.“Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some immeasurable, some of one name, some of various names, some similar, some dissimilar, some distinct, some confused. He asks the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and unconcealed. He asks the Saṅgha for drawing back to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha draws him back to the root for the intervening offenses by a lawful act, unalterable, and appropriate; they grant him combined probation in accordance with the Dhamma; but they grant him the period of penance and absolution contrary to the Dhamma. That monk, monks, is not purified from those offenses.”

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi.

“Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some immeasurable, some of one name, some of various names, some similar, some dissimilar, some distinct, some confused. He asks the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and concealed. He asks the Saṅgha for drawing back to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha draws him back to the root for the intervening offenses by a lawful act, unalterable, and appropriate; they grant him combined probation in accordance with the Dhamma; but they grant him the period of penance and absolution contrary to the Dhamma. That monk, monks, is not purified from those offenses.”

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi.

“Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some immeasurable, some of one name, some of various names, some similar, some dissimilar, some distinct, some confused. He asks the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable, both concealed and unconcealed. He asks the Saṅgha for drawing back to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha draws him back to the root for the intervening offenses by a lawful act, unalterable, and appropriate; they grant him combined probation in accordance with the Dhamma; but they grant him the period of penance and absolution contrary to the Dhamma. That monk, monks, is not purified from those offenses.”

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati aparimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo…pe… aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyo…pe… aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi …pe… parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi appaṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi.

“Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some immeasurable, some of one name, some of various names, some similar, some dissimilar, some distinct, some confused. He asks the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses—immeasurable, unconcealed; immeasurable, concealed; immeasurable, both concealed and unconcealed; measurable and immeasurable, unconcealed. He asks the Saṅgha for drawing back to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha draws him back to the root for the intervening offenses by a lawful act, unalterable, and appropriate; they grant him combined probation in accordance with the Dhamma; but they grant him the period of penance and absolution contrary to the Dhamma. That monk, monks, is not purified from those offenses.”

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; adhammena mānattaṃ deti, adhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi.

“Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some immeasurable, some of one name, some of various names, some similar, some dissimilar, some distinct, some confused. He asks the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and immeasurable, concealed. He asks the Saṅgha for drawing back to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha draws him back to the root for the intervening offenses by a lawful act, unalterable, and appropriate; they grant him combined probation in accordance with the Dhamma; but they grant him the period of penance and absolution contrary to the Dhamma. That monk, monks, is not purified from those offenses.”

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena; dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; adhammena mānattaṃ deti; adhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi.

“Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some immeasurable, some of one name, some of various names, some similar, some dissimilar, some distinct, some confused. He asks the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and immeasurable, both concealed and unconcealed. He asks the Saṅgha for drawing back to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha draws him back to the root for the intervening offenses by a lawful act, unalterable, and appropriate; they grant him combined probation in accordance with the Dhamma; but they grant him the period of penance and absolution contrary to the Dhamma. That monk, monks, is not purified from those offenses.”

Mūlāyaavisuddhinavakaṃ [samūlāvisuddhinavakaṃ (ka.)] niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Ninefold Section on Impurity Concerning the Root is finished.

### 10. Dutiyanavakaṃ ^10

> [!TIP]- Links to [[cv13-brahmali-pali#^10|Brahmali Version]] and BMC2 
> [[bmc2#^ch19|BMC Chapter 19]] and the following cites:
>  
> ```query
> "VIN-CV13.10" file:bmc2 -queryblock
> ```


 [idaṃ navakaṃ porāṇapotthakesu avisuddhivaseneva āgataṃ, vuccamānatatiyanavakena ca saṃsaṭṭhaṃ. taṃ paṭivisodhakehi asaṃsaṭṭhaṃ katvā visuṃ patiṭṭhāpitaṃ. sīhaḷasyāmapotthakesu pana taṃ visuddhivaseneva āgataṃ. taṃ panevaṃ veditabbaṃ –§10- mūlāyavisuddhinavaka (sī. syā.)§183. idha pana bhikkhave bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. so saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati, tassa tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, so parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo…pe… parimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyo…pe… parimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. so saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati, taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. so bhikkhave bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (1-3)§idha pana bhikkhave bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. so saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati, tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, so parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati aparimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo…pe… aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyo…pe… aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. so saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati, taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. so bhikkhave bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīti. (4-6)§idha pana bhikkhave bhikkhu sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjatī parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. so saṃghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati, tassa saṃgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, so parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṃghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi appaṭicchannāyo…pe… parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo…pe… parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. so saṃghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati, taṃ saṃgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. so bhikkhave bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (7-9)§mūlāya visuddhinavakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.]

10.The Second Group of Nines

183. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā appaṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (1)

183.Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses, some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some indistinct. He requests the Saṅgha for concurrent probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him concurrent probation for those offenses. While living on probation, he commits multiple additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, definite and unconcealed. He requests the Saṅgha for demotion to the root for these intervening offenses. The Saṅgha demotes him to the root for these intervening offenses through an unlawful, faulty, and inappropriate act; unlawfully grants concurrent probation; lawfully grants penance; and lawfully reinstates him. That monk, monks, is not purified of those offenses. (1)

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā paṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (2)

Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses, some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some indistinct. He requests the Saṅgha for concurrent probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him concurrent probation for those offenses. While living on probation, he commits multiple additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, definite and concealed. He requests the Saṅgha for demotion to the root for these intervening offenses. The Saṅgha demotes him to the root for these intervening offenses through an unlawful, faulty, and inappropriate act; unlawfully grants concurrent probation; lawfully grants penance; and lawfully reinstates him. That monk, monks, is not purified of those offenses. (2)

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (3)

Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses, some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some indistinct. He requests the Saṅgha for concurrent probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him concurrent probation for those offenses. While living on probation, he commits multiple additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, definite, both concealed and unconcealed. He requests the Saṅgha for demotion to the root for these intervening offenses. The Saṅgha demotes him to the root for these intervening offenses through an unlawful, faulty, and inappropriate act; unlawfully grants concurrent probation; lawfully grants penance; and lawfully reinstates him. That monk, monks, is not purified of those offenses. (3)

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi, ekanāmampi nānānāmampi, sabhāgampi visabhāgampi, vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati aparimāṇā appaṭicchannāyo…pe… aparimāṇā paṭicchannāyo…pe… aparimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi…pe… parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi appaṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (4-7)

Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses, some definite, some indefinite, some of one kind, some of various kinds, some similar, some dissimilar, some defined, some indistinct. He requests the Saṅgha for concurrent probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him concurrent probation for those offenses. While living on probation, he commits multiple additional Saṅghādisesa offenses—immeasurable, unconcealed... immeasurable, concealed... immeasurable, both concealed and unconcealed... definite and indefinite, unconcealed. He requests the Saṅgha for demotion to the root for these intervening offenses. The Saṅgha demotes him to the root for these intervening offenses through an unlawful, faulty, and inappropriate act; unlawfully grants concurrent probation; lawfully grants penance; and lawfully reinstates him. That monk, monks, is not purified of those offenses. (4-7)

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (8)

Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses, some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some indistinct. He requests the Saṅgha for concurrent probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him concurrent probation for those offenses. While living on probation, he commits multiple additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, definite and indefinite, concealed. He requests the Saṅgha for demotion to the root for these intervening offenses. The Saṅgha demotes him to the root for these intervening offenses through an unlawful, faulty, and inappropriate act; unlawfully grants concurrent probation; lawfully grants penance; and lawfully reinstates him. That monk, monks, is not purified of those offenses. (8)

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu avisuddho tāhi āpattīhi. (9)

Here, monks, a monk commits multiple Saṅghādisesa offenses, some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some indistinct. He requests the Saṅgha for concurrent probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him concurrent probation for those offenses. While living on probation, he commits multiple additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, definite and indefinite, both concealed and unconcealed. He requests the Saṅgha for demotion to the root for these intervening offenses. The Saṅgha demotes him to the root for these intervening offenses through an unlawful, faulty, and inappropriate act; unlawfully grants concurrent probation; lawfully grants penance; and lawfully reinstates him. That monk, monks, is not purified of those offenses. (9)

Dutiyanavakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Second Group of Nines is concluded.

### 11. Tatiyanavakaṃ ^11
