11.The third set of nine.

184. ‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. So tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati. Tassa evaṃ hoti – ‘ahaṃ kho sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāciṃ. Taṃ maṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ; dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhāna’nti. So saṅghaṃ purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ; dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānaṃ. Taṃ saṅgho purimāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti; dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi [ayaṃ paṭhamavāro sī syā. potthakesu paripuṇṇo dissati].

184.“Here, monks, a bhikkhu commits many Saṅghādisesa offenses, some measurable and some immeasurable… some definite and some indefinite. He asks the Saṅgha for compounded probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him compounded probation for those offenses. While living on probation, he commits many Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and unconcealed. He asks the Saṅgha to return him to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha returns him to the root for the intervening offenses by an unrighteous act, an invalid act, an unsuitable act, granting unlawful compounded probation. Thinking he is living on probation, he commits many Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and unconcealed. While standing in that state, he remembers the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses. He reflects: ‘I committed many Saṅghādisesa offenses, some measurable and some immeasurable… some definite and some indefinite. I asked the Saṅgha for compounded probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha granted me compounded probation for those offenses. While living on probation, I committed many Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and unconcealed. I asked the Saṅgha to return me to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha returned me to the root for the intervening offenses by an unrighteous act, an invalid act, an unsuitable act, granting me unlawful compounded probation. Thinking I was living on probation, I committed many Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and unconcealed. While standing in this state, I remember the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses. Why don’t I ask the Saṅgha to return me to the root for the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses by a righteous act, a valid act, a suitable act, granting lawful compounded probation, lawful penance, and lawful rehabilitation?’ He asks the Saṅgha to return him to the root for the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses by a righteous act, a valid act, a suitable act, granting lawful compounded probation, lawful penance, and lawful rehabilitation. The Saṅgha returns him to the root for the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses by a righteous act, a valid act, a suitable act; it grants him lawful compounded probation, grants him lawful penance, and rehabilitates him lawfully. Monks, that bhikkhu is purified of those offenses.”

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā paṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati, adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā paṭicchannāyo. So tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāāpattīnaṃ [purimānaṃ āpattīnaṃ (ka.)] antarāāpattiyo sarati, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati. Tassa evaṃ hoti – ‘ahaṃ kho sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇā paṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāciṃ. Taṃ maṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassi, adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇā paṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ purimāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparā āpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhāna’nti. So saṅghaṃ purimāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānaṃ. Taṃ saṅgho purimāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi.

“Here, monks, a bhikkhu commits many Saṅghādisesa offenses, some measurable and some immeasurable… some definite and some indefinite. He asks the Saṅgha for compounded probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him compounded probation for those offenses. While living on probation, he commits many Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and concealed. He asks the Saṅgha to return him to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha returns him to the root for the intervening offenses by an unrighteous act, an invalid act, an unsuitable act, granting unlawful compounded probation. Thinking he is living on probation, he commits many Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and concealed. While standing in that state, he remembers the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses. He reflects: ‘I committed many Saṅghādisesa offenses, some measurable and some immeasurable… some definite and some indefinite. I asked the Saṅgha for compounded probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha granted me compounded probation for those offenses. While living on probation, I committed many Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and concealed. I asked the Saṅgha to return me to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha returned me to the root for the intervening offenses by an unrighteous act, an invalid act, an unsuitable act, granting me unlawful compounded probation. Thinking I was living on probation, I committed many Saṅghādisesa offenses that are measurable and concealed. While standing in this state, I remember the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses. Why don’t I ask the Saṅgha to return me to the root for the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses by a righteous act, a valid act, a suitable act, granting lawful compounded probation, lawful penance, and lawful rehabilitation?’ He asks the Saṅgha to return him to the root for the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses by a righteous act, a valid act, a suitable act, granting lawful compounded probation, lawful penance, and lawful rehabilitation. The Saṅgha returns him to the root for the intervening offenses of the earlier offenses and the intervening offenses of the later offenses by a righteous act, a valid act, a suitable act; it grants him lawful compounded probation, grants him lawful penance, and rehabilitates him lawfully. Monks, that bhikkhu is purified of those offenses.”

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati. Tassa evaṃ hoti – ‘ahaṃ kho sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāciṃ. Taṃ maṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇā paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ purimāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhāna’nti. So saṅghaṃ purimāpattīnaṃ antarā āpattīnañca, aparā āpattīnaṃ antarā āpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānaṃ. Taṃ saṅgho purimāpattīnaṃ antarā āpattīnañca, aparā āpattīnaṃ antarā āpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits numerous Saṅghādisesa offenses—some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some mixed. He asks the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits numerous additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, whether definite or indefinite, whether concealed or unconcealed. He asks the Saṅgha for relegation to the root for the interim offenses. The Saṅgha relegates him to the root for the interim offenses through an unlawful, flawed, and unsuitable act, granting unlawful combined probation. Thinking, 'I am on probation,' he commits numerous additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, whether definite or indefinite, whether concealed or unconcealed. While standing on that ground, he recalls the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses. He reflects: 'I committed numerous Saṅghādisesa offenses—some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some mixed. I asked the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha granted me combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, I committed numerous additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, whether definite or indefinite, whether concealed or unconcealed. I asked the Saṅgha for relegation to the root for the interim offenses. The Saṅgha relegated me to the root for the interim offenses through an unlawful, flawed, and unsuitable act, granting unlawful combined probation. Thinking, "I am on probation," I committed numerous additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, whether definite or indefinite, whether concealed or unconcealed. While standing on that ground, I recall the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses. Why don’t I ask the Saṅgha for relegation to the root for both the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses through a lawful, unflawed, and suitable act, for lawful combined probation, lawful penance, and lawful reinstatement?' He asks the Saṅgha for relegation to the root for both the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses through a lawful, unflawed, and suitable act, for lawful combined probation, lawful penance, and lawful reinstatement. The Saṅgha relegates him to the root for both the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses through a lawful, unflawed, and suitable act, grants lawful combined probation, grants lawful penance, and lawfully reinstates him. That bhikkhu, bhikkhus, is purified of those offenses.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati aparimāṇāyo appaṭicchannāyo…pe… aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyo…pe… aparimāṇāyo paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi…pe… parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi appaṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasāmīti maññamāno…pe… taṃ saṅgho purimā āpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi [imepi cattāro vārā sī. syā. potthakesu paripuṇṇā dissanti].

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits numerous Saṅghādisesa offenses—some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some mixed. He asks the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits numerous additional Saṅghādisesa offenses: immeasurable and unconcealed... immeasurable and concealed... immeasurable, both concealed and unconcealed... definite and indefinite, unconcealed. He asks the Saṅgha for relegation to the root for the interim offenses. The Saṅgha relegates him to the root for the interim offenses through an unlawful, flawed, and unsuitable act, granting unlawful combined probation. Thinking, 'I am on probation,'... the Saṅgha then relegates him to the root for both the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses through a lawful, unflawed, and suitable act. It grants him lawful combined probation, lawful penance, and lawful reinstatement. That bhikkhu, bhikkhus, is purified of those offenses.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. So tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimā āpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati. Tassa evaṃ hoti – ‘ahaṃ kho sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāciṃ. Taṃ maṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyo. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimā āpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ purimā āpattīnaṃ antarā pattīnañca, aparāāpattīna antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhāna’nti. So saṅghaṃ purimā āpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānaṃ. Taṃ saṅgho purimā āpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi.

Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits numerous Saṅghādisesa offenses—some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some mixed. He asks the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits numerous additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, whether definite or indefinite, all concealed. He asks the Saṅgha for relegation to the root for these interim offenses. The Saṅgha relegates him to the root for these interim offenses through an unlawful, flawed, and unsuitable act, granting unlawful combined probation. Thinking, 'I am on probation,' he commits numerous additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, whether definite or indefinite, all concealed. While standing on that ground, he recalls the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses. He reflects: 'I committed numerous Saṅghādisesa offenses—some definite, some indefinite... some defined, some mixed. I asked the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha granted me combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, I committed numerous additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, whether definite or indefinite, all concealed. I asked the Saṅgha for relegation to the root for these interim offenses. The Saṅgha relegated me to the root for these interim offenses through an unlawful, flawed, and unsuitable act, granting unlawful combined probation. Thinking, "I am on probation," I committed numerous additional Saṅghādisesa offenses, whether definite or indefinite, all concealed. While standing on that ground, I recall the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses. Why don’t I ask the Saṅgha for relegation to the root for both the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses through a lawful, unflawed, and suitable act, for lawful combined probation, lawful penance, and lawful reinstatement?' He asks the Saṅgha for relegation to the root for both the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses through a lawful, unflawed, and suitable act, for lawful combined probation, lawful penance, and lawful reinstatement. The Saṅgha relegates him to the root for both the interim offenses among the earlier offenses and the interim offenses among the later offenses through a lawful, unflawed, and suitable act, grants lawful combined probation, grants lawful penance, and lawfully reinstates him. That bhikkhu, bhikkhus, is purified of those offenses.

‘‘Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. So saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yācati. Tassa saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yācati. Taṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassati adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti. So parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjati parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. So tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimā āpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarati. Tassa evaṃ hoti – ‘ahaṃ kho sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇampi aparimāṇampi…pe… vavatthitampi sambhinnampi. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ yāciṃ. Tassa me saṅgho tāsaṃ āpattīnaṃ samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasanto antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. Sohaṃ saṅghaṃ antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāciṃ. Taṃ maṃ saṅgho antarāāpattīnaṃ mūlāya paṭikassi adhammikena kammena kuppena aṭṭhānārahena, adhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ adāsi. Sohaṃ parivasāmīti maññamāno antarā sambahulā saṅghādisesā āpattiyo āpajjiṃ parimāṇāyopi aparimāṇāyopi paṭicchannāyopi appaṭicchannāyopi. Sohaṃ tasmiṃ bhūmiyaṃ ṭhito purimā āpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattiyo sarāmi. Yaṃnūnāhaṃ saṅghaṃ purimāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāyapaṭikassanaṃ yāceyyaṃ dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhāna’nti. So saṅghaṃ purimā āpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, aparāāpattīnaṃ antarāāpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassanaṃ yācati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ, dhammena mānattaṃ, dhammena abbhānaṃ. Taṃ saṅgho purimā āpattīnaṃ antarā āpattīnañca, aparā āpattīnaṃ antarā āpattīnañca, mūlāya paṭikassati dhammikena kammena akuppena ṭhānārahena, dhammena samodhānaparivāsaṃ deti, dhammena mānattaṃ deti, dhammena abbheti. So, bhikkhave, bhikkhu visuddho tāhi āpattīhi’’.

"Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu commits many Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some unmeasurable… some defined, some undefined. He requests the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha grants him combined probation for those offenses. While on probation, he commits many further Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some unmeasurable, some concealed, some unconcealed. He requests the Saṅgha to relegate him to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha relegates him to the root for the intervening offenses by an unlawful, invalid, unsuitable act, granting unlawful combined probation. Thinking he is undergoing probation, he commits many further Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some unmeasurable, some concealed, some unconcealed. While standing in that situation, he remembers the intervening offenses amongst the former offenses, and the intervening offenses amongst the latter offenses. He thinks: ‘I committed many Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some unmeasurable… some defined, some undefined. I requested the Saṅgha for combined probation for those offenses. The Saṅgha granted me combined probation for those offenses. While undergoing probation, I committed many further Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some unmeasurable, some concealed, some unconcealed. I requested the Saṅgha to relegate me to the root for the intervening offenses. The Saṅgha relegated me to the root for the intervening offenses by an unlawful, invalid, unsuitable act, granting me unlawful combined probation. Thinking I was undergoing probation, I committed many further Saṅghādisesa offenses—some measurable, some unmeasurable, some concealed, some unconcealed. While standing in that situation, I remember the intervening offenses amongst the former offenses, and the intervening offenses amongst the latter offenses. Why don’t I request the Saṅgha to relegate me to the root for the former offenses and the intervening offenses, as well as the latter offenses and the intervening offenses, by a lawful, valid, suitable act—lawful combined probation, lawful penance, and lawful reinstatement?’ He requests the Saṅgha to relegate him to the root for the former offenses and the intervening offenses, as well as the latter offenses and the intervening offenses, by a lawful, valid, suitable act—lawful combined probation, lawful penance, and lawful reinstatement. The Saṅgha relegates him to the root for the former offenses and the intervening offenses, as well as the latter offenses and the intervening offenses, by a lawful, valid, suitable act, grants him lawful combined probation, grants him lawful penance, and lawfully reinstates him. That bhikkhu, bhikkhus, is purified of those offenses."

Tatiyanavakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The third section of nine is completed.

Samuccayakkhandhako tatiyo.

The Third Chapter on Accumulations.

Tassuddānaṃ –

Its summary:

Appaṭicchannā ekāha-dvīha-tīha-catūha ca;Pañcāhapakkhadasannaṃ, āpattimāha mahāmuni.

Unconcealed for one, two, three, or four days; For five days, a fortnight, or a month, the Great Sage declared an offense.

Suddhanto ca vibbhamanto, parimāṇamukhaṃ dve bhikkhū;Tattha saññino dve yathā, vematikā tatheva ca.

From purity and straying, two bhikkhus at the limit of measure; There, two who are percipient, and likewise two who are doubtful.

Missakadiṭṭhino dve ca, asuddhakekadiṭṭhino;Dve ceva suddhadiṭṭhino.

Two who hold mixed views, two who hold singular impure views; And two who hold pure views.

Tatheva ca eko chādeti, atha makkhamatena ca;Ummattakadesanañca, mūlā aṭṭhārasa [pannarasa (ka.)] visuddhato.

Likewise, one conceals, then with a corrupt motive; And the preaching of the insane—these are the eighteen roots away from purity.

Ācariyānaṃ vibhajjapadānaṃ [vibhajjavādīnaṃ (sī.)], tambapaṇṇidīpapasādakānaṃ;Mahāvihāravāsīnaṃ, vācanā saddhammaṭṭhitiyāti.

Of the teachers who expound the distinctions, who inspired faith in Tambapaṇṇidīpa; residents of the Mahāvihāra, their recitation is for the stability of the true Dhamma.

Samuccayakkhandhakaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ.

The Chapter on Collected Items is concluded.
